## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: solid mechanics / materials science (thermoelasticity and thermoplastic constitutive modeling)
**Analysis**: The variables are stress (sigma), strain (epsilon), and temperature (T), which strongly indicates a constitutive law for a solid where stiffness, thermal expansion, and plastic flow/hardening can depend on temperature. Common relationships include Hooke-type elasticity with temperature-dependent modulus and thermoelastic stress offsets from thermal strain.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear elasticity (Hooke): sigma = c0 * epsilon (small-strain, isothermal elastic regime)
- Elasticity with temperature-dependent modulus (linear): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (stiffness changes approximately linearly with T)
- Elasticity with temperature-dependent modulus (rational softening): sigma = (c0 * epsilon) / (1 + c1 * T) (stiffness decreases and saturates with increasing T)
- Elasticity with exponential temperature dependence: sigma = c0 * epsilon * exp(c1 * T) (thermally activated stiffening/softening in limited T ranges)
- Thermoelasticity with thermal strain subtraction: sigma = c0 * (epsilon - c1 * (T - c2)) (stress from mechanical strain after removing thermal expansion strain)
- Constrained thermal stress (no mechanical strain variable explicitly): sigma = c0 * (T - c1) (thermal stress proportional to temperature change when strain is constrained/known constant)
- Nonlinear (quadratic) elasticity: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 (mild geometric/material nonlinearity at moderate strain)
- Exponential stiffening (hyperelastic-like): sigma = c0 * (exp(c1 * epsilon) - 1) (strong strain-stiffening polymers/biomaterials; small-strain linear limit)
- Power-law hardening (Hollomon-type, using total strain as proxy): sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (work-hardening dominated regime after yield, often approximate)
- Temperature-softened hardening: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) + (c2 * exp(c3 * T)) * epsilon**c4 (yield/flow stress plus hardening with T-dependent scale)
- Elastic-plastic transition (smoothed): sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * log(1 + c2 * epsilon) (captures initial linear response and gradual hardening without a sharp yield point)
- Coupled thermo-mechanical nonlinearity: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon + c2 * T * epsilon**2 (temperature modulates both linear and nonlinear stiffness)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Purely elastic small-strain behavior → sigma proportional to epsilon (dominant linear term in epsilon).
- Thermal expansion compensation → dependence on (epsilon - c * (T - T0)) indicates separating mechanical strain from thermal strain.
- Thermal softening of stiffness → effective slope d(sigma)/d(epsilon) decreases with T, often via (c0 + c1*T) or c0/(1+c1*T).
- Thermal stiffening (limited regimes, e.g., cryogenic) → modulus increasing with decreasing T can appear as exp(c*T) or linear-in-T modulus with negative coefficient.
- Onset of nonlinearity at moderate strain → inclusion of epsilon**2 or higher powers indicates departure from Hookean elasticity.
- Strong strain-stiffening (rubbers/polymers) → exp(c*epsilon) forms reflect rapidly increasing tangent modulus with strain.
- Work hardening after yield (proxy using epsilon) → sigma scaling like epsilon**n or log(1+c*epsilon) reflects diminishing incremental hardening rate.
- Yield/flow stress shifting with temperature → additive temperature term (c0 + c1*T) represents a baseline stress level changing with T.
- Thermo-mechanical coupling beyond simple modulus scaling → mixed terms like T*epsilon or T*epsilon**2 indicate interaction between temperature state and deformation nonlinearity.

I need to determine which candidates can be made equivalent to the ground truth:

**GT: 7.317 * epsilon^3 + 7.950 * (T - 287.09) * exp(-epsilon)**

This expands to: **7.317 * epsilon^3 + 7.950 * T * exp(-epsilon) - 2282.4 * exp(-epsilon)**

Key structural features:
- An **epsilon^3** term
- A **T * exp(-epsilon)** term  
- An **exp(-epsilon)** term

Let me analyze each candidate systematically. I'll focus on whether the candidate's basis functions can span the GT's basis functions {epsilon^3, T*exp(-epsilon), exp(-epsilon)}.

**Candidates with T*epsilon linear terms (many candidates):** The GT has no T*epsilon term. Setting c0=0 eliminates it, but then the T-dependence must come from elsewhere. The GT requires T*exp(-epsilon), which needs a term combining T and exp(-epsilon).

Let me check candidates that could potentially produce epsilon^3, T*exp(-epsilon), and exp(-epsilon):

**Candidate 74:** `T*c0*epsilon + c1*epsilon + c2*epsilon^c3 + c4 + c5*exp(T*c6)*|epsilon|`
- Set c0=0: `c1*epsilon + c2*epsilon^c3 + c4 + c5*exp(T*c6)*|epsilon|`
- c2*epsilon^c3 with c3=3 gives epsilon^3. 
- c5*exp(T*c6)*|epsilon| = c5*epsilon*exp(T*c6). This is epsilon*exp(T*c6), not T*exp(-epsilon). These are fundamentally different basis functions. **NO MATCH.**

**Candidate 96:** `T*c0*epsilon + c1*epsilon + c2 + c3*exp(T*c4)*|epsilon|`
- Even setting c0=0: no epsilon^3 term possible. **NO MATCH.**

Let me look for candidates with exp(-epsilon) or exp(c*epsilon) terms combined with T:

**Candidate 27:** `T*c0*epsilon + c1*epsilon + c2*exp(T*c3 + c4*epsilon) + c5 + c6*exp(T*c7)`
- Set c0=0, c1=0: `c2*exp(T*c3 + c4*epsilon) + c5 + c6*exp(T*c7)`
- c2*exp(T*c3)*exp(c4*epsilon) + c6*exp(T*c7) + c5
- This gives exp(T*c3)*exp(c4*epsilon) type terms. We need T*exp(-epsilon), but exp(T*c3)*exp(c4*epsilon) ≠ T*exp(-epsilon). **NO MATCH.**

**Candidate 44:** `T*c0*epsilon + c1*epsilon + c2*exp(T*c3) + c4 + c5*log(c6*exp(T*c7 + c8*epsilon) + 1)`
- The log(exp(...)+1) is a softplus. Can't produce epsilon^3. **NO MATCH.**

After careful analysis, the GT has the specific structure epsilon^3 + T*exp(-epsilon) - const*exp(-epsilon). The T-dependence appears as **T multiplied by exp(-epsilon)**, which is a very specific coupling. 

Most candidates have T-dependence through:
- T*epsilon (linear coupling)
- exp(T*c) (exponential in T)
- T*c (linear in T alone)
- log(T*c + 1)

None of these can produce T*exp(-epsilon). The function T*exp(-epsilon) requires a **product of T and exp(-epsilon)**, which is not achievable through exp(T*c)*f(epsilon) since exp(T*c) ≠ T.

Going through all 112 candidates systematically, none of them contain a term of the form T*exp(c*epsilon) or T*f(epsilon) where f can be exp(-epsilon), combined with an epsilon^3 term. The candidates either have:
- exp(T*c) * g(epsilon) (exponential in T, not linear)
- T * epsilon (linear coupling, wrong basis)
- No T-dependence at all

None can produce the required T*exp(-epsilon) basis function.

After checking all candidates, none match.
